## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a reactant concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. Classical rate laws relate dA/dt to powers of A, and more complex mechanisms (autocatalysis, enzyme kinetics, reversible reactions) introduce nonlinear dependencies.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- Fractional/general n-th order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (generalized rate law with arbitrary reaction order)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (n-th order with constant source/sink term)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Second-order with linear term: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (competing first and second order pathways)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis, A reacts with product)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or effective third-order process)
- Quadratic with constant: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (polynomial rate with source term)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or aging kinetics)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * (c1 - A) (cubic autocatalytic mechanism)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure power-law dependence on concentration (dA/dt ~ A^n) indicates a simple elementary reaction of order n
- A polynomial in A (quadratic or cubic) often signals competing parallel reaction pathways or autocatalytic mechanisms
- Rational functions of A (A/(c+A)) indicate saturation or enzyme-mediated kinetics where a catalyst is involved
- Linear dependence dA/dt = c0*A + c1 suggests a reversible first-order reaction approaching equilibrium
- Products of A with (c - A) indicate conservation laws where A + B = constant, reducing a two-species system to one variable
- Explicit time dependence beyond what A(t) provides suggests externally driven conditions (temperature ramp, light intensity change)
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not explicitly on t, the system is autonomous and standard rate law forms apply
- Negative coefficient on the leading A term indicates consumption; positive constant terms indicate a source or feed of reactant
- Half-integer or fractional powers of A suggest chain reaction mechanisms or surface reaction kinetics
- Multiple additive terms in A with different powers suggest a composite mechanism with elementary steps of different molecularity

**GT:** `-0.3122*A*exp(-0.0798*t) + 0.4717*sin(0.8722*A)`

The GT has two terms:
1. `A*exp(α*t)` where α < 0
2. `sin(β*A)` (no phase shift, no offset)

Let me analyze each candidate by checking if extra terms can be zeroed out and if the core structure matches.

- It's `c_a * A * exp(c_b * t) + c_c * sin(c_d * A)`
- No constant offset, no A² terms, no A³ terms, no log terms, no extra exponentials
- The sin term has NO phase shift (c4 = 0 is allowed if candidates have `sin(A*c3 + c4)`)
